<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Woundedknee1891.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1330" data-file-width="1843" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Woundedknee1891.jpg/220px-Woundedknee1891.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Woundedknee1891.jpg/330px-Woundedknee1891.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Woundedknee1891.jpg/440px-Woundedknee1891.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Woundedknee1891.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A mass grave being dug for frozen bodies from the 1890 <a href="/wiki/Wounded_Knee_Massacre" title="Wounded Knee Massacre">Wounded Knee Massacre</a>, in which the U.S. Army killed 150 <a href="/wiki/Lakota_people" title="Lakota people">Lakota people</a>, marking the end of the <a href="/wiki/American_Indian_Wars" title="American Indian Wars">American Indian Wars</a></div></div></div>
<p>Debates over the origins of racism often suffer from a lack of clarity over the term. Many use the term "racism" to refer to more general phenomena, such as <a href="/wiki/Xenophobia" title="Xenophobia">xenophobia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethnocentrism" title="Ethnocentrism">ethnocentrism</a>, although scholars attempt to clearly distinguish those phenomena from racism as an <a href="/wiki/Ideology" title="Ideology">ideology</a> or from scientific racism, which has little to do with ordinary xenophobia. Others conflate recent forms of racism with earlier forms of ethnic and national conflict. In most cases, ethno-national conflict seems to owe itself to conflict over land and strategic resources. In some cases, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnicity" title="Ethnicity">ethnicity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a> were harnessed in order to rally <a href="/wiki/Combatant" title="Combatant">combatants</a> in wars between great religious empires (for example, the Muslim Turks and the Catholic Austro-Hungarians).
</p><p>Notions of race and racism have often played central roles in <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_conflict" title="Ethnic conflict">ethnic conflicts</a>. Throughout history, when an adversary is identified as "other" based on notions of race or ethnicity (in particular when "other" is interpreted to mean "inferior"), the means employed by the self-presumed "superior" party to appropriate territory, human chattel, or material wealth often have been more ruthless, more brutal, and less constrained by <a href="/wiki/Morality" title="Morality">moral</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ethics" title="Ethics">ethical</a> considerations. According to historian Daniel Richter, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontiac%27s_Rebellion" title="Pontiac's Rebellion">Pontiac's Rebellion</a> saw the emergence on both sides of the conflict of "the novel idea that all Native people were 'Indians,' that all Euro-Americans were 'Whites,' and that all on one side must unite to destroy the other".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Basil_Davidson" title="Basil Davidson">Basil Davidson</a> states in his documentary, <i>Africa: Different but Equal</i>, that racism, in fact, only just recently surfaced as late as the 19th century, due to the need for a justification for slavery in the Americas.
</p><p>Historically, racism was a major driving force behind the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transatlantic_slave_trade" title="Transatlantic slave trade">Transatlantic slave trade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> It was also a major force behind <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation" title="Racial segregation">racial segregation</a>, especially in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> in the nineteenth and early twentieth centuries, and South Africa under <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>; 19th and 20th century racism in the <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western world</a> is particularly well documented and constitutes a reference point in studies and discourses about racism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-8">[8]</a></sup> Racism has played a role in <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocides</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_genocide" title="Armenian genocide">Armenian genocide</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">Holocaust</a>, and colonial projects like the European <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Colonization of the Americas">colonization of the Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colonisation_of_Africa" title="Colonisation of Africa">Africa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Western_imperialism_in_Asia" title="Western imperialism in Asia">Asia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">Indigenous peoples</a> have been—and are—often subject to racist attitudes. Practices and ideologies of racism are condemned by the United Nations in the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Declaration of Human Rights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_and_racial_nationalism">Ethnic and racial nationalism</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_nationalism" title="Ethnic nationalism">Ethnic nationalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racial_nationalism" title="Racial nationalism">Racial nationalism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Romantic_nationalism" title="Romantic nationalism">Romantic nationalism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Keep_Australia_White.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1942" data-file-width="1488" decoding="async" height="287" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Keep_Australia_White.jpg/220px-Keep_Australia_White.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Keep_Australia_White.jpg/330px-Keep_Australia_White.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Keep_Australia_White.jpg/440px-Keep_Australia_White.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Keep_Australia_White.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1917 anti-<a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> propaganda leaflet imploring voters to "<a href="/wiki/White_Australia_policy" title="White Australia policy">keep Australia white</a>". A horde of Asians bearing a dragon flag is shown to the north.</div></div></div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, Europe was confronted with the new "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nationalities" title="Nationalities">nationalities</a> question", leading to reconfigurations of the European map, on which the frontiers between the states had been delineated during the 1648 <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Westphalia" title="Peace of Westphalia">Peace of Westphalia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">Nationalism</a> had made its first appearance with the invention of the <i><a href="/wiki/Lev%C3%A9e_en_masse" title="Levée en masse">levée en masse</a></i> by the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolutionaries</a>, thus inventing mass <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> in order to be able to defend the newly founded <a href="/wiki/French_First_Republic" title="French First Republic">Republic</a> against the <i><a href="/wiki/Ancien_R%C3%A9gime" title="Ancien Régime">Ancien Régime</a></i> order represented by the European monarchies. This led to the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a> (1792–1802) and then to the conquests of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>, and to the subsequent European-wide debates on the concepts and realities of <a href="/wiki/Nation" title="Nation">nations</a>, and in particular of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nation-state" title="Nation-state">nation-states</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westphalia_Treaty" title="Westphalia Treaty">Westphalia Treaty</a> had divided Europe into various empires and kingdoms (such as the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Empire" title="Swedish Empire">Swedish Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">Kingdom of France</a>, etc.), and for centuries wars were waged between princes (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kabinettskriege" title="Kabinettskriege">Kabinettskriege</a></i> in German).
</p><p>Modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nation-state" title="Nation-state">nation-states</a> appeared in the wake of the French Revolution, with the formation of <a href="/wiki/Patriotism" title="Patriotism">patriotic</a> sentiments for the first time in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enlightenment_Spain" title="Enlightenment Spain">Spain</a> during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peninsula_War" title="Peninsula War">Peninsula War</a> (1808–1813, known in Spain as the Independence War). Despite the restoration of the previous order with the 1815 <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a>, the "nationalities question" became the main problem of Europe during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_Era" title="Industrial Era">Industrial Era</a>, leading in particular to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1848_Revolutions" title="1848 Revolutions">1848 Revolutions</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_unification" title="Italian unification">Italian unification</a> completed during the 1871 <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a>, which itself culminated in the proclamation of the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> in the Hall of Mirrors in the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Versailles" title="Palace of Versailles">Palace of Versailles</a>, thus achieving the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_unification" title="German unification">German unification</a>.
</p><p>Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, the "<a href="/wiki/Sick_man_of_Europe" title="Sick man of Europe">sick man of Europe</a>", was confronted with endless nationalist movements, which, along with the dissolving of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austrian-Hungarian_Empire" title="Austrian-Hungarian Empire">Austrian-Hungarian Empire</a>, would lead to the creation, after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, of the various nation-states of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balkan" title="Balkan">Balkans</a>, with "national <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minorities" title="Minorities">minorities</a>" in their borders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ethnic_nationalism" title="Ethnic nationalism">Ethnic nationalism</a>, which advocated the belief in a hereditary membership of the nation, made its appearance in the historical context surrounding the creation of the modern nation-states.
</p><p>One of its main influences was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romantic_nationalist" title="Romantic nationalist">Romantic nationalist</a> movement at the turn of the 19th century, represented by figures such as <a href="/wiki/Johann_Gottfried_Herder" title="Johann Gottfried Herder">Johann Herder</a> (1744–1803), <a href="/wiki/Johann_Gottlieb_Fichte" title="Johann Gottlieb Fichte">Johan Fichte</a> (1762–1814) in the <i>Addresses to the German Nation</i> (1808), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Friedrich_Hegel" title="Friedrich Hegel">Friedrich Hegel</a> (1770–1831), or also, in France, <a href="/wiki/Jules_Michelet" title="Jules Michelet">Jules Michelet</a> (1798–1874). It was opposed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberal_nationalism" title="Liberal nationalism">liberal nationalism</a>, represented by authors such as <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Renan" title="Ernest Renan">Ernest Renan</a> (1823–1892), who conceived of the nation as a community, which, instead of being based on the <i><a href="/wiki/Volk" title="Volk">Volk</a></i> ethnic group and on a specific, common language, was founded on the subjective will to live together ("the nation is a daily <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plebiscite" title="Plebiscite">plebiscite</a>", 1882) or also <a href="/wiki/John_Stuart_Mill" title="John Stuart Mill">John Stuart Mill</a> (1806–1873).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup>
Ethnic nationalism blended with scientific racist discourses, as well as with "continental <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperialist" title="Imperialist">imperialist</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Hannah_Arendt" title="Hannah Arendt">Hannah Arendt</a>, 1951<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arendt_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Arendt-110">[110]</a></sup>) discourses, for example in the <a href="/wiki/Pan-Germanism" title="Pan-Germanism">pan-Germanism</a> discourses, which postulated the racial superiority of the German <i><a href="/wiki/Volk" title="Volk">Volk</a></i> (people/folk). The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alldeutscher_Verband" title="Alldeutscher Verband">Pan-German League</a> (<i>Alldeutscher Verband</i>), created in 1891, promoted <a href="/wiki/German_colonial_empire" title="German colonial empire">German imperialism</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Racial_hygiene" title="Racial hygiene">racial hygiene</a>", and was opposed to intermarriage with <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>. Another popular current, the <i><a href="/wiki/V%C3%B6lkisch_movement" title="Völkisch movement">Völkisch movement</a></i>, was also an important proponent of the German ethnic nationalist discourse, and it combined Pan-Germanism with modern <a href="/wiki/Racial_antisemitism" title="Racial antisemitism">racial antisemitism</a>. Members of the Völkisch movement, in particular the <a href="/wiki/Thule_Society" title="Thule Society">Thule Society</a>, would participate in the founding of the <a href="/wiki/German_Workers%27_Party" title="German Workers' Party">German Workers' Party</a> (DAP) in Munich in 1918, the predecessor of the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a>. Pan-Germanism played a decisive role in the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">interwar period</a> of the 1920s–1930s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arendt_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-Arendt-110">[110]</a></sup>
</p><p>These currents began to associate the idea of the nation with the biological concept of a "<a href="/wiki/Master_race" title="Master race">master race</a>" (often the "<a href="/wiki/Aryan_race" title="Aryan race">Aryan race</a>" or the "<a href="/wiki/Nordic_race" title="Nordic race">Nordic race</a>") issued from the scientific racist discourse. They conflated nationalities with ethnic groups, called "races", in a radical distinction from previous racial discourses that posited the existence of a "race struggle" inside the nation and the state itself. Furthermore, they believed that political boundaries should mirror these alleged racial and ethnic groups, thus justifying <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a>, in order to achieve "racial purity" and also to achieve ethnic homogeneity in the nation-state.
</p><p>Such racist discourses, combined with nationalism, were not, however, limited to pan-Germanism. In France, the transition from Republican liberal nationalism, to ethnic nationalism, which made nationalism a characteristic of <a href="/wiki/History_of_far-right_movements_in_France" title="History of far-right movements in France">far-right movements in France</a>, took place during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dreyfus_Affair" title="Dreyfus Affair">Dreyfus Affair</a> at the end of the 19th century. During several years, a nationwide crisis affected French society, concerning the alleged treason of <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Dreyfus" title="Alfred Dreyfus">Alfred Dreyfus</a>, a French Jewish military officer. The country polarized itself into two opposite camps, one represented by <a href="/wiki/%C3%89mile_Zola" title="Émile Zola">Émile Zola</a>, who wrote <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J%27Accuse%E2%80%A6!" title="J'Accuse…!">J'Accuse…!</a></i> in defense of Alfred Dreyfus, and the other represented by the nationalist poet, <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Barr%C3%A8s" title="Maurice Barrès">Maurice Barrès</a> (1862–1923), one of the founders of the ethnic nationalist discourse in France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> At the same time, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Maurras" title="Charles Maurras">Charles Maurras</a> (1868–1952), founder of the monarchist <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Action_fran%C3%A7aise" title="Action française">Action française</a></i> movement, theorized the "anti-France", composed of the "four confederate states of Protestants, Jews, Freemasons and foreigners" (his actual word for the latter being the pejorative <i><a href="/wiki/Metic" title="Metic">métèques</a></i>). Indeed, to him the first three were all "internal foreigners", who threatened the ethnic unity of the <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French people</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History"><span class="anchor" id="In_history"></span>History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"History of racism" redirects here. For racism concept in history, see <a href="/wiki/Historical_race_concepts" title="Historical race concepts">historical race concepts</a>.</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnocentrism_and_proto-racism">Ethnocentrism and proto-racism</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ksenophontov_noah.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1134" data-file-width="862" decoding="async" height="289" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Ksenophontov_noah.jpg/220px-Ksenophontov_noah.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Ksenophontov_noah.jpg/330px-Ksenophontov_noah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Ksenophontov_noah.jpg/440px-Ksenophontov_noah.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ksenophontov_noah.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Genesis" title="Book of Genesis">Book of Genesis</a>'s biblical curse on <a href="/wiki/Canaan_(son_of_Ham)" title="Canaan (son of Ham)">Canaan</a>, which was often misinterpreted as <a href="/wiki/Curse_of_Ham" title="Curse of Ham">a curse on his father</a> <a href="/wiki/Ham_(son_of_Noah)" title="Ham (son of Noah)">Ham</a>, was used to justify <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">slavery in 19th century America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aristotle">Aristotle</span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bernard_Lewis" title="Bernard Lewis">Bernard Lewis</a> has cited the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_philosophy" title="Greek philosophy">Greek philosopher</a> <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a> who, in his discussion of slavery, stated that while Greeks are free by nature, "<a href="/wiki/Barbarian" title="Barbarian">barbarians</a>" (non-Greeks) are slaves by nature, in that it is in their nature to be more willing to submit to a <a href="/wiki/Despotism" title="Despotism">despotic</a> government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis-113">[113]</a></sup> Though Aristotle does not specify any particular races, he argues that people from nations outside Greece are more prone to the burden of slavery than those from <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greece</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> While Aristotle makes remarks about the most natural slaves being those with strong bodies and slave souls (unfit for rule, unintelligent) which would seem to imply a physical basis for discrimination, he also explicitly states that the right kind of souls and bodies do not always go together, implying that the greatest determinate for inferiority and natural slaves versus natural masters is the soul, not the body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> This proto-racism is seen as an important precursor to modern racism by classicist <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Isaac" title="Benjamin Isaac">Benjamin Isaac</a>.
</p><p>Such proto-racism and ethnocentrism must be looked at within context, because a modern understanding of racism based on hereditary inferiority (with modern racism based on <a href="/wiki/Eugenics" title="Eugenics">eugenics</a> and scientific racism) was not yet developed and it is unclear whether Aristotle believed the natural inferiority of Barbarians was caused by environment and climate (like many of his contemporaries) or by birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup>
</p><p>Historian Dante A. Puzzo, in his discussion of Aristotle, racism, and the ancient world writes that:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<blockquote><p>Racism rests on two basic assumptions: that a correlation exists between physical characteristics and moral qualities; that mankind is divisible into superior and inferior stocks. Racism, thus defined, is a modern conception, for prior to the XVIth century there was virtually nothing in the life and thought of the West that can be described as racist. To prevent misunderstanding a clear distinction must be made between racism and <a href="/wiki/Ethnocentrism" title="Ethnocentrism">ethnocentrism</a> ... The Ancient <a href="/wiki/Hebrews" title="Hebrews">Hebrews</a>, in referring to all who were not Hebrews as <a href="/wiki/Gentile" title="Gentile">Gentiles</a>, were indulging in ethnocentrism, not in racism. ... So it was with the <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Hellenes</a> who denominated all non-Hellenes—whether the wild <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Egyptians" title="Egyptians">Egyptians</a> whom they acknowledged as their mentors in the arts of <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a>—Barbarians, the term denoting that which was strange or foreign.</p></blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_Arab_writers">Medieval Arab writers</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Arab_attitudes_to_Black_people" title="Medieval Arab attitudes to Black people">Medieval Arab attitudes to Black people</a></div>
<p>Bernard Lewis has also cited historians and geographers of the <a href="/wiki/MENA" title="MENA">Middle East and North Africa</a> region,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis53_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis53-118">[118]</a></sup> including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Muqaddasi" title="Al-Muqaddasi">Al-Muqaddasi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Jahiz" title="Al-Jahiz">Al-Jahiz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Masudi" title="Al-Masudi">Al-Masudi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abu_Rayhan_Biruni" title="Abu Rayhan Biruni">Abu Rayhan Biruni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nasir_al-Din_al-Tusi" title="Nasir al-Din al-Tusi">Nasir al-Din al-Tusi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Qutaybah" title="Ibn Qutaybah">Ibn Qutaybah</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis53_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis53-118">[118]</a></sup> Though the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qur%27an" title="Qur'an">Qur'an</a> expresses no racial prejudice, Lewis argues that ethnocentric prejudice later developed among <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">Arabs</a>, for a variety of reasons:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis53_118-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis53-118">[118]</a></sup> their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim_conquests" title="Muslim conquests">extensive conquests</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">slave trade</a>; the influence of <a href="/wiki/Aristotelianism" title="Aristotelianism">Aristotelian</a> ideas regarding slavery, which some <a href="/wiki/Early_Islamic_philosophy" title="Early Islamic philosophy">Muslim philosophers</a> directed towards <a href="/wiki/Zanj" title="Zanj">Zanj</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tlosfea_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tlosfea-119">[119]</a></sup>) and <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic peoples</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis-113">[113]</a></sup> and the influence of <a href="/wiki/Judeo-Christian" title="Judeo-Christian">Judeo-Christian</a> ideas regarding divisions among humankind.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> By the eighth century, anti-black prejudice among Arabs resulted in discrimination. A number of medieval Arabic authors argued against this prejudice, urging respect for all black people and especially <a href="/wiki/Ethiopians" title="Ethiopians">Ethiopians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> By the 14th century, a significant number of slaves came from <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a>; Lewis argues that this led to the likes of Egyptian historian Al-Abshibi (1388–1446) writing that "[i]t is said that when the [black] slave is sated, he fornicates, when he is hungry, he steals."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> According to Lewis, the 14th-century Tunisian scholar <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Khaldun" title="Ibn Khaldun">Ibn Khaldun</a> also wrote:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis53_118-3"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis53-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colorq_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-colorq-123">[123]</a></sup>
</p>
<blockquote><p>...beyond [known peoples of black West Africa] to the south there is no civilization in the proper sense. There are only humans who are closer to dumb animals than to rational beings. They live in thickets and caves, and eat herbs and unprepared grain. They frequently eat each other. They cannot be considered human beings. Therefore, the Negro nations are, as a rule, submissive to slavery, because (Negroes) have little that is (essentially) human and possess attributes that are quite similar to those of dumb animals, as we have stated.</p></blockquote>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Wesleyan_University" title="Wesleyan University">Wesleyan University</a> professor Abdelmajid Hannoum, French <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orientalists" title="Orientalists">Orientalists</a> projected racist and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonialist" title="Colonialist">colonialist</a> views of the 19th century into their translations of medieval Arabic writings, including those of Ibn Khaldun. This resulted in the translated texts <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Racializing" title="Racializing">racializing</a> Arabs and <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berber</a> people, when no such distinction was made in the originals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> James E. Lindsay argues that the concept of an <a href="/wiki/Arab_nationalism" title="Arab nationalism">Arab identity</a> itself did not exist until modern times,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> though others like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Hoyland" title="Robert Hoyland">Robert Hoyland</a> have argued that a common sense of <a href="/wiki/Arab_identity" title="Arab identity">Arab identity</a> already existed by the 9th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Limpieza_de_sangre"><i>Limpieza de sangre</i></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Limpieza_de_sangre" title="Limpieza de sangre">Limpieza de sangre</a></div>
<p>With the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">Umayyad Caliphate's conquest of Hispania</a>, Muslim Arabs and <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berbers</a> overthrew the previous <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigothic</a> rulers and created <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Al-Andalus</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> which contributed to the <a href="/wiki/Golden_age_of_Jewish_culture_in_Spain" title="Golden age of Jewish culture in Spain">Golden age of Jewish culture</a>, and lasted for six centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> It was followed by the centuries-long <i><a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> terminated under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reyes_Catolicos" title="Reyes Catolicos">Catholic monarchs</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferdinand_V_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand V of Spain">Ferdinand V</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Spain" title="Isabella I of Spain">Isabella I</a>. The legacy Catholic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_people" title="Spanish people">Spaniards</a> then formulated the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleanliness_of_blood" title="Cleanliness of blood">Cleanliness of blood</a></i> doctrine. It was during this time in history that the Western concept of aristocratic "<a href='/wiki/Nobility#"Blue"_blood' title="Nobility">blue blood</a>" emerged in a racialized, religious and feudal context,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-130">[130]</a></sup> so as to stem the upward social mobility of the converted <a href="/wiki/Converso" title="Converso">New Christians</a>. Robert Lacey explains:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup>
</p>
<blockquote>
<p>It was the Spaniards who gave the world the notion that an aristocrat's blood is not red but blue. The Spanish nobility started taking shape around the ninth century in classic military fashion, occupying land as warriors on horseback. They were to continue the process for more than five hundred years, clawing back sections of the peninsula from its Moorish occupiers, and a nobleman demonstrated his pedigree by holding up his sword arm to display the filigree of blue-blooded veins beneath his pale skin—proof that his birth had not been contaminated by the dark-skinned enemy. Sangre azul, blue blood, was thus a euphemism for being a <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">white</a> man—Spain's own particular reminder that the refined footsteps of the aristocracy through history carry the rather less refined spoor of racism.
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Following the expulsion of the Arabic <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a> and most of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sephardic_Jews" title="Sephardic Jews">Sephardic Jews</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iberian_peninsula" title="Iberian peninsula">Iberian peninsula</a>, the remaining <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> were forced to <a href="/wiki/Converso" title="Converso">convert</a> to Roman Catholicism, becoming "<a href="/wiki/New_Christian" title="New Christian">New Christians</a>", who were sometimes discriminated against by the "<a href="/wiki/Old_Christian" title="Old Christian">Old Christians</a>" in some cities (including <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">Toledo</a>), despite condemnations by the Church and the State, which both welcomed the new flock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-130">[130]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Inquisition" title="Inquisition">Inquisition</a> was carried out by members of the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Order" title="Dominican Order">Dominican Order</a> in order to weed out the converts who still practiced <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> in secret. The system and ideology of the <i>limpieza de sangre</i> ostracized false Christian converts from society in order to protect it against <a href="/wiki/Treason" title="Treason">treason</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> The remnants of such legislation persevered into the 19th century in military contexts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, the legal distinction between New and Old Christian was only ended through a legal decree issued by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marquis_of_Pombal" title="Marquis of Pombal">Marquis of Pombal</a> in 1772, almost three centuries after the implementation of the racist discrimination. The <i>limpieza de sangre</i> legislation was common also during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">colonization of the Americas</a>, where it led to the racial and feudal separation of peoples and social strata in the colonies. It was however often ignored in practice, as the new colonies needed skilled people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:De_Bry_1c.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="869" data-file-width="1021" decoding="async" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/De_Bry_1c.JPG/220px-De_Bry_1c.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/De_Bry_1c.JPG/330px-De_Bry_1c.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/De_Bry_1c.JPG/440px-De_Bry_1c.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:De_Bry_1c.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 16th-century illustration by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_Revolt#Protestantism" title="Dutch Revolt">Flemish Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Theodor_de_Bry" title="Theodor de Bry">Theodor de Bry</a> for <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_de_las_Casas" title="Bartolomé de las Casas">Las Casas</a>'s <i>Brevisima relación de la destrucción de las Indias</i>, depicting Spanish atrocities during the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cuba#Spanish_conquest_and_early_colonization_(1492_-_1800)" title="History of Cuba">conquest of Cuba</a></div></div></div>
<p>At the end of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Renaissance" title="Spanish Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Valladolid_debate" title="Valladolid debate">Valladolid debate</a> (1550–1551), concerning the treatment of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_people_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous people of the Americas">natives</a> of the "<a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>" pitted the Dominican friar and Bishop of Chiapas, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_de_Las_Casas" title="Bartolomé de Las Casas">Bartolomé de Las Casas</a>, to another Dominican and Humanist <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosopher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Gin%C3%A9s_de_Sep%C3%BAlveda" title="Juan Ginés de Sepúlveda">Juan Ginés de Sepúlveda</a>. The latter argued that the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Indians</a> practiced <a href="/wiki/Human_sacrifice" title="Human sacrifice">human sacrifice</a> of innocents, <a href="/wiki/Cannibalism" title="Cannibalism">cannibalism</a>, and other such "crimes against nature"; they were unacceptable and should be suppressed by any means possible including war,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> thus reducing them to slavery or serfdom was in accordance with Catholic theology and <a href="/wiki/Natural_law" title="Natural law">natural law</a>. To the contrary, Bartolomé de Las Casas argued that the Amerindians were free men in the natural order and deserved the same treatment as others, according to <a href="/wiki/Catholic_theology" title="Catholic theology">Catholic theology</a>. It was one of the many controversies concerning racism, slavery, religion, and European morality that would arise in the following centuries and which resulted in the legislation protecting the natives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hernandez_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hernandez-136">[136]</a></sup> The marriage between Luisa de Abrego, a free black domestic servant from Seville and Miguel Rodríguez, a white segovian conquistador in 1565 in St. Augustine (Spanish Florida), is the first known and recorded Christian marriage anywhere in the continental United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the Spanish colonies, Spaniards developed a complex <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castas" title="Castas">caste system</a> based on race, which was used for social control, and which also determined a person's importance in society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Acuña-p23-24_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Acuña-p23-24-138">[138]</a></sup> While many Latin American countries have long since rendered the system officially illegal through legislation, usually at the time of their independence, <a href="/wiki/Prejudice" title="Prejudice">prejudice</a> based on degrees of perceived racial distance from European ancestry combined with one's socioeconomic status remain, an echo of the colonial caste system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Racism_as_a_modern_phenomenon">Racism as a modern phenomenon</span></h3>
<p>Although <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">antisemitism</a> has a long history, related to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egyptian_religion" title="Ancient Egyptian religion">native Egyptian</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_religion" title="Ancient Greek religion">Greek religions</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Anti-Judaism" title="Anti-Judaism">anti-Judaism</a>), racism itself is sometimes described as a <i>modern</i> phenomenon. In the view of the French philosopher and historian <a href="/wiki/Michel_Foucault" title="Michel Foucault">Michel Foucault</a>, the first formulation of racism emerged in the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_Europe" title="Early modern Europe">Early Modern period</a> as the "<a href="/wiki/Discourse" title="Discourse">discourse</a> of race struggle", and a historical and political discourse, which Foucault opposed to the philosophical and juridical discourse of <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> On the other hand, e.g. Chinese self-identification as a "yellow race" predated such European racial concepts.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>This European analysis, which first appeared in <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Great Britain</a>, was then carried on in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> by such people as <a href="/wiki/Henri_de_Boulainvilliers" title="Henri de Boulainvilliers">Boulainvilliers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Fr%C3%A9ret" title="Nicolas Fréret">Nicolas Fréret</a>, and then, during the 1789 <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emmanuel-Joseph_Siey%C3%A8s" title="Emmanuel-Joseph Sieyès">Sieyès</a>, and afterwards, <a href="/wiki/Augustin_Thierry" title="Augustin Thierry">Augustin Thierry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Augustin_Cournot" title="Antoine Augustin Cournot">Cournot</a>. Boulainvilliers, who created the matrix of such racist discourse in <a href="/wiki/France_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="France in the Middle Ages">medieval France</a>, conceived of the "race" as being something closer to the sense of a "nation", that is, in his time, the "race" meant the "people".
</p><p>He conceived of France as being divided between various nations—the unified <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nation-state" title="Nation-state">nation-state</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Anachronism" title="Anachronism">anachronism</a> here—which themselves formed different "races". Boulainvilliers opposed the <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a>, which tried to bypass the <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy" title="Aristocracy">aristocracy</a> by establishing a direct relationship to the <a href="/wiki/Estates_General_(France)" title="Estates General (France)">Third Estate</a>. Thus, he developed the theory that the French aristocrats were the descendants of foreign invaders, whom he called the "<a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>", while according to him, the Third Estate constituted the autochthonous, vanquished <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallo-Romans" title="Gallo-Romans">Gallo-Romans</a>, who were dominated by the Frankish aristocracy as a consequence of the <a href="/wiki/Right_of_conquest" title="Right of conquest">right of conquest</a>. Early modern racism was opposed to nationalism and the nation-state: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Dominique_de_Reynaud_de_Montlosier" title="François Dominique de Reynaud de Montlosier">Comte de Montlosier</a>, in exile during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, who borrowed Boulainvilliers' discourse on the "Nordic race" as being the French aristocracy that invaded the plebeian "Gauls", thus showed his contempt for the Third Estate, calling it "this new people born of slaves ... <a href="/wiki/Miscegenation" title="Miscegenation">mixture of all races and of all times</a>".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Advert_for_Pears%27_Soap_Wellcome_L0030380.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6637" data-file-width="4376" decoding="async" height="334" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Advert_for_Pears%27_Soap_Wellcome_L0030380.jpg/220px-Advert_for_Pears%27_Soap_Wellcome_L0030380.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Advert_for_Pears%27_Soap_Wellcome_L0030380.jpg/330px-Advert_for_Pears%27_Soap_Wellcome_L0030380.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Advert_for_Pears%27_Soap_Wellcome_L0030380.jpg/440px-Advert_for_Pears%27_Soap_Wellcome_L0030380.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Advert_for_Pears%27_Soap_Wellcome_L0030380.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Advertisement for <a href="/wiki/Pears_(soap)" title="Pears (soap)">Pears' Soap</a> Caption reads, "Matchless for the complexion..." Illustration of 'before and after' use of soap by black child in the bath; soap washes off his dark complexion.</div></div></div>
<p>While 19th-century racism became closely intertwined with nationalism,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> leading to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_nationalist" title="Ethnic nationalist">ethnic nationalist</a> discourse that identified the "race" with the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volk_(German_word)" title="Volk (German word)">folk</a>", leading to such movements as <a href="/wiki/Pan-Germanism" title="Pan-Germanism">pan-Germanism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pan-Turkism" title="Pan-Turkism">pan-Turkism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pan-Arabism" title="Pan-Arabism">pan-Arabism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pan-Slavism" title="Pan-Slavism">pan-Slavism</a>, medieval racism precisely divided the nation into various non-biological "races", which were thought to be the consequence of historical conquests and <a href="/wiki/Social_conflict" title="Social conflict">social conflicts</a>. Michel Foucault traced the genealogy of modern racism to this medieval "historical and political discourse of race struggle". According to him, it divided itself in the 19th century according to two rival lines: on one hand, it was incorporated by racists, biologists and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eugenicists" title="Eugenicists">eugenicists</a>, who gave it the modern sense of "race", and they also transformed this popular discourse into a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_racism" title="State racism">state racism</a>" (e.g., Nazism). On the other hand, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxists" title="Marxists">Marxism</a> also seized this discourse founded on the assumption of a political struggle that provided the real <a href="/wiki/Philosophy_of_history" title="Philosophy of history">engine of history</a> and continued to act underneath the apparent peace. Thus, Marxists transformed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Essentialist" title="Essentialist">essentialist</a> notion of "race" into the historical notion of "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_struggle" title="Class struggle">class struggle</a>", defined by socially structured positions: capitalist or proletarian. In <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Will_to_Knowledge" title="The Will to Knowledge">The Will to Knowledge</a></i> (1976), Foucault analyzed another opponent of the "race struggle" discourse: <a href="/wiki/Sigmund_Freud" title="Sigmund Freud">Sigmund Freud</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Psychoanalysis" title="Psychoanalysis">psychoanalysis</a>, which opposed the concept of "blood <a href="/wiki/Heredity" title="Heredity">heredity</a>", prevalent in the 19th century racist discourse.
</p><p>Authors such as <a href="/wiki/Hannah_Arendt" title="Hannah Arendt">Hannah Arendt</a>, in her 1951 book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Origins_of_Totalitarianism" title="The Origins of Totalitarianism">The Origins of Totalitarianism</a></i>, have said that the racist ideology (<i>popular racism</i>) which developed at the end of the 19th century helped legitimize the <a href="/wiki/New_Imperialism" title="New Imperialism">imperialist conquests</a> of foreign territories and the atrocities that sometimes accompanied them (such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herero_and_Namaqua_Genocide" title="Herero and Namaqua Genocide">Herero and Namaqua Genocide</a> of 1904–1907 or the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_genocide" title="Armenian genocide">Armenian genocide</a> of 1915–1917). <a href="/wiki/Rudyard_Kipling" title="Rudyard Kipling">Rudyard Kipling</a>'s poem, <i><a href="/wiki/The_White_Man%27s_Burden" title="The White Man's Burden">The White Man's Burden</a></i> (1899), is one of the more famous illustrations of the belief in the inherent superiority of the <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">European culture</a> over the rest of the world, though it is also thought to be a satirical appraisal of such imperialism. Racist ideology thus helped legitimize the conquest and incorporation of foreign territories into an empire, which were regarded as a humanitarian obligation partially as a result of these racist beliefs.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scientific_racism_irish.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1020" decoding="async" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Scientific_racism_irish.jpg/220px-Scientific_racism_irish.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Scientific_racism_irish.jpg/330px-Scientific_racism_irish.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Scientific_racism_irish.jpg/440px-Scientific_racism_irish.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scientific_racism_irish.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A late-19th-century illustration from <i>Ireland from One or Two Neglected Points of View</i> by H. Strickland Constable shows an alleged similarity between "Irish Iberian" and "Negro" features in contrast to the "higher" "Anglo-Teutonic".</div></div></div>
<p>However, during the 19th century, Western European colonial powers were involved in the suppression of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">Arab slave trade</a> in Africa,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> as well as in the suppression of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a> in West Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> Some Europeans during the time period objected to injustices that occurred in some colonies and lobbied on behalf of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aboriginal_peoples" title="Aboriginal peoples">aboriginal peoples</a>. Thus, when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saartjie_Baartman" title="Saartjie Baartman">Hottentot Venus</a> was displayed in England in the beginning of the 19th century, the African Association publicly opposed itself to the exhibition. The same year that Kipling published his poem, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Conrad" title="Joseph Conrad">Joseph Conrad</a> published <i><a href="/wiki/Heart_of_Darkness" title="Heart of Darkness">Heart of Darkness</a></i> (1899), a clear criticism of the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a>, which was owned by <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium" title="Leopold II of Belgium">Leopold II of Belgium</a>.
</p><p>Examples of racial theories used include the creation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamitic" title="Hamitic">Hamitic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethno-linguistic" title="Ethno-linguistic">ethno-linguistic</a> group during the <a href="/wiki/European_exploration_of_Africa" title="European exploration of Africa">European exploration of Africa</a>. It was then restricted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karl_Friedrich_Lepsius" title="Karl Friedrich Lepsius">Karl Friedrich Lepsius</a> (1810–1877) to non-<a href="/wiki/Semitic_languages" title="Semitic languages">Semitic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Asiatic_languages" title="Afro-Asiatic languages">Afro-Asiatic languages</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup>
</p><p>The term <i>Hamite</i> was applied to different populations within North Africa, mainly comprising Ethiopians, <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Eritrea" title="Demographics of Eritrea">Eritreans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Somali_people" title="Somali people">Somalis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berber_people" title="Berber people">Berbers</a>, and the ancient Egyptians. Hamites were regarded as Caucasoid peoples who probably originated in either Arabia or Asia on the basis of their cultural, physical and linguistic similarities with the peoples of those areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> Europeans considered Hamites to be more civilized than <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">Sub-Saharan Africans</a>, and more akin to themselves and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semitic_peoples" title="Semitic peoples">Semitic peoples</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> In the first two-thirds of the 20th century, the Hamitic race was, in fact, considered one of the branches of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_race" title="Caucasian race">Caucasian race</a>, along with the <a href="/wiki/Aryan_race" title="Aryan race">Indo-Europeans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Semitic_people" title="Semitic people">Semites</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_race" title="Mediterranean race">Mediterraneans</a>.
</p><p>However, the Hamitic peoples themselves were often deemed to have failed as rulers, which was usually ascribed to <a href="/wiki/Miscegenation" title="Miscegenation">interbreeding</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Negroe" title="Negroe">Negroes</a>. In the mid-20th century, the German scholar <a href="/wiki/Carl_Meinhof" title="Carl Meinhof">Carl Meinhof</a> (1857–1944) claimed that the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> race was formed by a merger of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamitic" title="Hamitic">Hamitic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Negroid" title="Negroid">Negro</a> races. The Hottentots (<a href="/wiki/Nama_people" title="Nama people">Nama</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khoi" title="Khoi">Khoi</a>) were formed by the merger of Hamitic and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bushmen" title="Bushmen">Bushmen</a> (San) races—both being termed nowadays as <a href="/wiki/Khoisan" title="Khoisan">Khoisan</a> peoples.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Freedman%27s_bureau.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1148" data-file-width="1455" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Freedman%27s_bureau.jpg/220px-Freedman%27s_bureau.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Freedman%27s_bureau.jpg/330px-Freedman%27s_bureau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Freedman%27s_bureau.jpg/440px-Freedman%27s_bureau.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Freedman%27s_bureau.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One in a series of posters attacking <a href="/wiki/Radical_Republicans" title="Radical Republicans">Radical Republicans</a> on the issue of black suffrage, issued during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_gubernatorial_election,_1866" title="Pennsylvania gubernatorial election, 1866">Pennsylvania gubernatorial election of 1866</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the United States in the early 19th century, the <a href="/wiki/American_Colonization_Society" title="American Colonization Society">American Colonization Society</a> was established as the primary vehicle for proposals to return black Americans to greater freedom and equality in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> The colonization effort resulted from a mixture of motives with its founder <a href="/wiki/Henry_Clay" title="Henry Clay">Henry Clay</a> stating that "unconquerable prejudice resulting from their color, they never could amalgamate with the free whites of this country. It was desirable, therefore, as it respected them, and the residue of the population of the country, to drain them off".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> Racism spread throughout the New World in the late 19th century and early 20th century. <a href="/wiki/Whitecapping" title="Whitecapping">Whitecapping</a>, which started in Indiana in the late 19th century, soon spread throughout all of North America, causing many African laborers to flee from the land they worked on. In the US, during the 1860s, racist posters were used during election campaigns. In one of these racist posters (see above), a black man is depicted lounging idly in the foreground as one white man ploughs his field and another chops wood. Accompanying labels are: "In the sweat of thy face shalt thou eat thy bread", and "The white man must work to keep his children and pay his taxes." The black man wonders, "Whar is de use for me to work as long as dey make dese appropriations." Above in a cloud is an image of the "Freedman's Bureau! Negro Estimate of Freedom!" The bureau is pictured as a large domed building resembling the U.S. Capitol and is inscribed "Freedom and No Work". Its columns and walls are labeled, "Candy", "Rum, Gin, Whiskey", "Sugar Plums", "Indolence", "White Women", "Apathy", "White Sugar", "Idleness", and so on.
</p><p>On June 5, 1873, Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Galton" title="Francis Galton">Francis Galton</a>, distinguished English explorer and cousin of Charles Darwin, wrote in a letter to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i>:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>My proposal is to make the encouragement of <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Chinese</a> settlements of Africa a part of our national policy, in the belief that the Chinese immigrants would not only maintain their position, but that they would multiply and their descendants supplant the inferior Negro race ... I should expect that the African seaboard, now sparsely occupied by lazy, palavering savages, might in a few years be tenanted by industrious, order-loving Chinese, living either as a semidetached dependency of China, or else in perfect freedom under their own law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Racial_policy_of_Nazi_Germany" title="Racial policy of Nazi Germany">Racial policy of Nazi Germany</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holocaust" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forced_settlements_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Forced settlements in the Soviet Union">Forced settlements in the Soviet Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">Apartheid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation_in_the_United_States" title="Racial segregation in the United States">Racial segregation in the United States</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">Rwandan genocide</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Austrian_Nazis_and_local_residents_watch_as_Jews_are_forced_to_scrub_the_pavement_after_Nazi_annexation.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2696" data-file-width="3800" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Austrian_Nazis_and_local_residents_watch_as_Jews_are_forced_to_scrub_the_pavement_after_Nazi_annexation.jpg/220px-Austrian_Nazis_and_local_residents_watch_as_Jews_are_forced_to_scrub_the_pavement_after_Nazi_annexation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Austrian_Nazis_and_local_residents_watch_as_Jews_are_forced_to_scrub_the_pavement_after_Nazi_annexation.jpg/330px-Austrian_Nazis_and_local_residents_watch_as_Jews_are_forced_to_scrub_the_pavement_after_Nazi_annexation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Austrian_Nazis_and_local_residents_watch_as_Jews_are_forced_to_scrub_the_pavement_after_Nazi_annexation.jpg/440px-Austrian_Nazis_and_local_residents_watch_as_Jews_are_forced_to_scrub_the_pavement_after_Nazi_annexation.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Austrian_Nazis_and_local_residents_watch_as_Jews_are_forced_to_scrub_the_pavement_after_Nazi_annexation.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Austrian Nazis and local residents watch as Jews are forced to scrub the pavement, Vienna, March 1938</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WannseeList.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="757" data-file-width="514" decoding="async" height="324" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/WannseeList.jpg/220px-WannseeList.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/WannseeList.jpg/330px-WannseeList.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/WannseeList.jpg/440px-WannseeList.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WannseeList.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Adolf_Eichmann" title="Adolf Eichmann">Eichmann</a>'s list of the Jewish population in Europe, drafted for the <a href="/wiki/Wannsee_Conference" title="Wannsee Conference">Wannsee Conference</a>, held to ensure the cooperation of various levels of the Nazi government in the <a href="/wiki/Final_Solution" title="Final Solution">Final Solution</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%22Colored%22_drinking_fountain_from_mid-20th_century_with_african-american_drinking.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3618" data-file-width="5276" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/%22Colored%22_drinking_fountain_from_mid-20th_century_with_african-american_drinking.jpg/220px-%22Colored%22_drinking_fountain_from_mid-20th_century_with_african-american_drinking.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/%22Colored%22_drinking_fountain_from_mid-20th_century_with_african-american_drinking.jpg/330px-%22Colored%22_drinking_fountain_from_mid-20th_century_with_african-american_drinking.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/%22Colored%22_drinking_fountain_from_mid-20th_century_with_african-american_drinking.jpg/440px-%22Colored%22_drinking_fountain_from_mid-20th_century_with_african-american_drinking.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%22Colored%22_drinking_fountain_from_mid-20th_century_with_african-american_drinking.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Drinking_fountain" title="Drinking fountain">drinking fountain</a> from the mid-20th century labelled "Colored" with an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American">African-American</a> man drinking</div></div></div>
<p>The Nazi party, which seized power in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_federal_election,_March_1933" title="German federal election, March 1933">1933 German elections</a> and maintained a dictatorship over much of Europe until the <a href="/wiki/End_of_World_War_II_in_Europe" title="End of World War II in Europe">End of World War II on the European continent</a>, deemed the Germans to be part of an Aryan "<a href="/wiki/Master_race" title="Master race">master race</a>" (<i>Herrenvolk</i>), who therefore had the right to expand their territory and enslave or kill members of other races deemed inferior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup>
</p><p>The racial ideology conceived by the Nazis graded humans on a scale of pure Aryan to non-Aryan, with the latter viewed as subhuman. At the top of the scale of pure Aryans were Germans and other Germanic peoples including the Dutch, Scandinavians, and the <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a> as well as other peoples such as some northern Italians and the French, who were said to have a suitable admixture of Germanic blood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davies06_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davies06-154">[154]</a></sup> Nazi policies labeled <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">people of color</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> (mainly <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">Czechs</a>) as inferior non-Aryan subhumans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Operation_Barbarossa_2004_page_180_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Operation_Barbarossa_2004_page_180-155">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-156">[156]</a></sup> Jews were at the bottom of the hierarchy, considered inhuman and thus <a href="/wiki/Life_unworthy_of_life" title="Life unworthy of life">unworthy of life</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECurta20019,_26–30_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECurta20019,_26–30-161">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> In accordance with Nazi racial ideology, approximately six million Jews were killed in the <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">Holocaust</a>. 2.5 million <a href="/wiki/Nazi_crimes_against_the_Polish_nation" title="Nazi crimes against the Polish nation">ethnic Poles</a>, 0.5 million <a href="/wiki/Genocide_of_Serbs_in_the_Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Genocide of Serbs in the Independent State of Croatia">ethnic Serbs</a> and 0.2–0.5 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porajmos" title="Porajmos">Romani</a> were killed by the regime and its collaborators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Nazis considered most <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> to be non-Aryan <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Untermenschen" title="Untermenschen">Untermenschen</a></i>. The Nazi Party's chief racial theorist, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Rosenberg" title="Alfred Rosenberg">Alfred Rosenberg</a>, adopted the term from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Klansman" title="Klansman">Klansman</a> <a href="/wiki/Lothrop_Stoddard" title="Lothrop Stoddard">Lothrop Stoddard</a>'s 1922 book <i>The Revolt Against Civilization: The Menace of the Under-man</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> In the secret plan <a href="/wiki/Generalplan_Ost" title="Generalplan Ost">Generalplan Ost</a> ("Master Plan East") the Nazis resolved to expel, enslave, or exterminate most Slavic people to provide "<a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">living space</a>" for Germans,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gumkowski_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gumkowski-165">[165]</a></sup> but Nazi policy towards Slavs changed during World War II due to manpower shortages which necessitated limited Slavic participation in the <a href="/wiki/Waffen-SS" title="Waffen-SS">Waffen-SS</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norman_Davies_Pp._167,_209_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Norman_Davies_Pp._167,_209-166">[166]</a></sup> Significant war crimes were committed against Slavs, particularly <a href="/wiki/Nazi_crimes_against_the_Polish_nation" title="Nazi crimes against the Polish nation">Poles</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_mistreatment_of_Soviet_prisoners_of_war" title="German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war">Soviet POWs</a> had a far higher mortality rate than their American and British counterparts due to deliberate neglect and mistreatment. Between June 1941 and January 1942, the Nazis killed an estimated 2.8 million <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> POWs, whom they viewed as "subhuman".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the years 1943–1945, around 120,000 Polish people, mostly women and children, became the victims of <a href="/wiki/Massacres_of_Poles_in_Volhynia_and_Eastern_Galicia" title="Massacres of Poles in Volhynia and Eastern Galicia">ethnicity-based massacres</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Insurgent_Army" title="Ukrainian Insurgent Army">Ukrainian Insurgent Army</a>, which was then operating in the territory of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Poland_(1939%E2%80%9345)" title="Occupation of Poland (1939–45)">occupied Poland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-no_simple_victory_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-no_simple_victory-168">[168]</a></sup> In addition to Poles who represented the vast majority of the murdered people, the victims also included Jews, Armenians, Russians, and Ukrainians who were married to Poles or attempted to help them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ZZWRP0_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-ZZWRP0-169">[169]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the intensification of ties with Nazi Germany in the 1930s, <a href="/wiki/Ante_Paveli%C4%87" title="Ante Pavelić">Ante Pavelić</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Usta%C5%A1e" title="Ustaše">Ustaše</a> and their idea of the <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croatian nation</a> became increasingly race-oriented.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kallis_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kallis-170">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Payne_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-Payne-172">[172]</a></sup> The Ustaše view of national and racial identity, as well as the theory of <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a> as an inferior race, was influenced by <a href="/wiki/Croatian_nationalism" title="Croatian nationalism">Croatian nationalists</a> and intellectuals from the end of the 19th and the beginning of the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kallis_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kallis-170">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> Serbs were primary targets of racial laws and murders in the puppet <a href="/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Independent State of Croatia">Independent State of Croatia</a> (NDH); Jews and Roma were also targeted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> The Ustaše introduced laws to strip Serbs of their citizenship, livelihoods, and possessions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Genocide_of_Serbs_in_the_Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Genocide of Serbs in the Independent State of Croatia">genocide</a> in the NDH, Serbs suffered among the highest casualty rates in Europe during the World War II, and the NDH was one of the most lethal regimes in the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Payne_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-Payne-172">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>German praise for America's institutional racism was continuous throughout the early 1930s, and Nazi lawyers were advocates of the use of American models.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whitman_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-Whitman-180">[180]</a></sup> Race based U.S. citizenship laws and <a href="/wiki/Anti-miscegenation_laws" title="Anti-miscegenation laws">anti-miscegenation laws</a> (no race mixing) directly inspired the Nazi's two principal <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">Nuremberg racial laws</a>—the Citizenship Law and the Blood Law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whitman_180-1"><a href="#cite_note-Whitman-180">[180]</a></sup> Hitler's 1925 memoir <i><a href="/wiki/Mein_Kampf" title="Mein Kampf">Mein Kampf</a></i> was full of admiration for America's treatment of "coloreds".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> Nazi expansion eastward was accompanied with invocation of America's colonial expansion westward, with the accompanying actions toward the Native Americans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Westermann_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-Westermann-182">[182]</a></sup> In 1928, Hitler praised Americans for having "gunned down the millions of Redskins to a few hundred thousand, and now keeps the modest remnant under observation in a cage."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> On Nazi Germany's expansion eastward, in 1941 Hitler stated, "Our Mississippi [the line beyond which Thomas Jefferson wanted all Indians expelled] must be the Volga."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Westermann_182-1"><a href="#cite_note-Westermann-182">[182]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:No_beer_sold_to_indians.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="717" data-file-width="973" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/No_beer_sold_to_indians.jpg/220px-No_beer_sold_to_indians.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/No_beer_sold_to_indians.jpg/330px-No_beer_sold_to_indians.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/No_beer_sold_to_indians.jpg/440px-No_beer_sold_to_indians.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:No_beer_sold_to_indians.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A sign posted above a bar that reads "No beer sold to Indians [Native Americans]". <a href="/wiki/Birney,_Montana" title="Birney, Montana">Birney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a>, 1941.</div></div></div>
<p>White supremacy was dominant in the U.S. from its founding up to the <a href="/wiki/Civil_rights_movement" title="Civil rights movement">civil rights movement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> On the U.S. immigration laws prior to 1965, sociologist Stephen Klineberg cited the law as clearly declaring "that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_European" title="Northern European">Northern Europeans</a> are a superior subspecies of the white race."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Immigration_law_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-Immigration_law-185">[185]</a></sup> While anti-Asian racism was embedded in U.S. politics and culture in the early 20th century, <a href="/wiki/Indian_people" title="Indian people">Indians</a> were also racialized for their anticolonialism, with U.S. officials, casting them as a "Hindu" menace, pushing for Western imperial expansion abroad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Naturalization_Act_of_1790" title="Naturalization Act of 1790">Naturalization Act of 1790</a> limited U.S. citizenship to whites only, and in the 1923 case, <i><a href="/wiki/United_States_v._Bhagat_Singh_Thind" title="United States v. Bhagat Singh Thind">United States v. Bhagat Singh Thind</a></i>, the Supreme Court ruled that high caste Hindus were not "white persons" and were therefore racially ineligible for naturalized citizenship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> It was after the <a href="/wiki/Luce%E2%80%93Celler_Act_of_1946" title="Luce–Celler Act of 1946">Luce–Celler Act of 1946</a> that a quota of 100 Indians per year could immigrate to the U.S. and become citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Immigration_and_Nationality_Act_of_1965" title="Immigration and Nationality Act of 1965">Immigration and Nationality Act of 1965</a> dramatically opened entry to the U.S. to immigrants other than traditional Northern European and <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic groups</a>, and as a result would significantly alter the demographic mix in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Immigration_law_185-1"><a href="#cite_note-Immigration_law-185">[185]</a></sup>
</p><p>Serious <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Durban_Riot" title="Durban Riot">race riots in Durban</a> between <a href="/wiki/Indian_South_Africans" title="Indian South Africans">Indians</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zulus" title="Zulus">Zulus</a> erupted in 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ne_Win" title="Ne Win">Ne Win</a>'s rise to power in Burma in 1962 and his relentless persecution of "resident aliens" led to an exodus of some 300,000 <a href="/wiki/Burmese_Indians" title="Burmese Indians">Burmese Indians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> They migrated to escape <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Racial_Discrimination_against_Burmese_Indians" title="Racial Discrimination against Burmese Indians">racial discrimination</a> and wholesale nationalisation of private enterprises a few years later, in 1964.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_Revolution" title="Zanzibar Revolution">Zanzibar Revolution</a> of January 12, 1964, put an end to the local <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">Arab</a> dynasty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt13jan_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-nyt13jan-193">[193]</a></sup> Thousands of Arabs and Indians
