in Zanzibar were massacred in riots, and thousands more were detained or fled the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> In August 1972, Ugandan President <a href="/wiki/Idi_Amin" title="Idi Amin">Idi Amin</a> started the expropriation of properties owned by Asians and Europeans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> In the same year, Amin ethnically cleansed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_Asians_in_Uganda_in_1972" title="Expulsion of Asians in Uganda in 1972">Uganda's Asians</a>, giving them 90 days to leave the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup>
Shortly after World War II, the South African <a href="/wiki/National_Party_(South_Africa)" title="National Party (South Africa)">National Party</a> took control of the government in South Africa. Between 1948 and 1994, the <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> regime took place. This regime based its ideology on the racial separation of whites and non-whites, including the unequal rights of non-whites. Several protests and violence occurred during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_resistance_to_South_African_apartheid" title="Internal resistance to South African apartheid">struggle against apartheid</a>, the most famous of these include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sharpeville_Massacre" title="Sharpeville Massacre">Sharpeville Massacre</a> in 1960, the <a href="/wiki/Soweto_uprising" title="Soweto uprising">Soweto uprising</a> in 1976, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Church_Street_bombing" title="Church Street bombing">Church Street bombing</a> of 1983, and the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town_peace_march" title="Cape Town peace march">Cape Town peace march</a> of 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary">Contemporary</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Julius_Malema_2011-09-14.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2100" data-file-width="3150" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Julius_Malema_2011-09-14.jpg/220px-Julius_Malema_2011-09-14.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Julius_Malema_2011-09-14.jpg/330px-Julius_Malema_2011-09-14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Julius_Malema_2011-09-14.jpg/440px-Julius_Malema_2011-09-14.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Julius_Malema_2011-09-14.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>On 12 September 2011, <a href="/wiki/Julius_Malema" title="Julius Malema">Julius Malema</a>, the youth leader of South Africa's ruling <a href="/wiki/African_National_Congress" title="African National Congress">ANC</a>, was found guilty of hate speech for singing "<a href='/wiki/South_African_farm_attacks#"Shoot_the_boer"_controversy' title="South African farm attacks">Shoot the Boer</a>" at a number of public events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Congo Civil War</a> (1998–2003), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pygmy_people" title="Pygmy people">Pygmy people</a> were hunted down like game animals and eaten. Both sides in the war regarded them as "subhuman" and some say their flesh can confer magical powers. UN human rights activists reported in 2003 that rebels had carried out acts of <a href="/wiki/Cannibalism" title="Cannibalism">cannibalism</a>. Sinafasi Makelo, a representative of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mbuti" title="Mbuti">Mbuti</a> pygmies, has asked the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" title="UN Security Council">UN Security Council</a> to recognise cannibalism as both a <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crime against humanity</a> and an act of <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> A report released by the United Nations Committee on the Elimination of Racial Discrimination condemns <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>'s treatment of the '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bushmen" title="Bushmen">Bushmen</a>' as racist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> In 2008, the tribunal of the 15-nation Southern African Development Community (SADC) accused Zimbabwean President <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mugabe" title="Robert Mugabe">Robert Mugabe</a> of having a racist attitude towards white people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing_Anti-African_protests" title="Nanjing Anti-African protests">mass demonstrations and riots</a> against African students in <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a>, China, lasted from December 1988 to January 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> In November 2009, British newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> reported that <a href="/wiki/Lou_Jing" title="Lou Jing">Lou Jing</a>, of mixed Chinese and African parentage, had emerged as the most famous talent show contestant in China and has become the subject of intense debate because of her skin color.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-205">[205]</a></sup> Her attention in the media opened serious debates about <a href="/wiki/Racism_in_China" title="Racism in China">racism in China</a> and racial prejudice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some 70,000 black African Mauritanians were expelled from Mauritania in the late 1980s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> In the Sudan, black African captives in the civil war were often <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_contemporary_Africa" title="Slavery in contemporary Africa">enslaved</a>, and female prisoners were often sexually abused.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darfur_conflict" title="Darfur conflict">Darfur conflict</a> has been described by some as a racial matter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> In October 2006, Niger announced that it would deport the approximately 150,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> Arabs living in the <a href="/wiki/Diffa" title="Diffa">Diffa</a> region of eastern Niger to Chad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> While the government collected Arabs in preparation for the <a href="/wiki/Deportation" title="Deportation">deportation</a>, two girls died, reportedly after fleeing Government forces, and three women suffered miscarriages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fiji-0050.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2321" data-file-width="3557" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Fiji-0050.JPG/220px-Fiji-0050.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Fiji-0050.JPG/330px-Fiji-0050.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Fiji-0050.JPG/440px-Fiji-0050.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fiji-0050.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The burnt out remains of Govinda's Indian Restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>, May 2000</div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jakarta_riots_of_May_1998" title="Jakarta riots of May 1998">Jakarta riots of May 1998</a> <a href="/wiki/Discrimination_against_Chinese_Indonesians" title="Discrimination against Chinese Indonesians">targeted</a> many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Indonesian" title="Chinese Indonesian">Chinese Indonesians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-Chinese_legislation_in_Indonesia" title="Anti-Chinese legislation in Indonesia">anti-Chinese legislation</a> was in the Indonesian constitution until 1998. Resentment against <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a> workers has led to violent confrontations in Africa<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> and Oceania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NZ_Herald_229612_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-NZ_Herald_229612-218">[218]</a></sup> Anti-Chinese rioting, involving tens of thousands of people,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> broke out in <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> in May 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indians_in_Fiji" title="Indians in Fiji">Indo-Fijians</a> suffered violent attacks after the <a href="/wiki/2000_Fijian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2000 Fijian coup d'état">Fiji coup in 2000</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> Non-indigenous citizens of Fiji are subject to discrimination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> Racial divisions also exist in Guyana,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> Malaysia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> Trinidad and Tobago,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> Madagascar,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> and South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> In Malaysia such racist state policies are codified on many levels,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> see <a href="/wiki/Bumiputera_(Malaysia)" title="Bumiputera (Malaysia)">Bumiputera</a>.
</p><p>Peter Bouckaert, the <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>'s emergencies director, said in an interview that "racist hatred" is the chief motivation behind the <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims_in_Myanmar" title="Persecution of Muslims in Myanmar">violence against Rohingya Muslims</a> in <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup>
</p><p>One form of racism in the United States was enforced <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation_in_the_United_States" title="Racial segregation in the United States">racial segregation</a>, which existed until the 1960s, when it was outlawed in the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964" title="Civil Rights Act of 1964">Civil Rights Act of 1964</a>. It has been argued that this separation of races continues to exist <i>de facto</i> today in different forms, such as lack of access to loans and resources or discrimination by police and other government officials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2016 <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research poll</a> found that Italians, in particular, hold strong <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-Romanyism" title="Anti-Romanyism">anti-Romani views</a>, with 82% of Italians expressing negative opinions about <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani</a>. In Greece, there are 67%, in Hungary, 64%, in France, 61%, in Spain, 49%, in Poland, 47%, in the UK, 45%, in Sweden, 42%, in Germany, 40%, and in the Netherlands, 37%, that have an unfavourable view of Roma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> A survey conducted by <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> found the Czech Republic, Lithuania, Belarus and Ukraine had the strongest racial bias against black people in Europe, while Serbia, Slovenia and Bosnia and Herzegovina had the weakest racial bias, followed by Croatia and Ireland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_racism">Scientific racism</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scientific_racism" title="Scientific racism">Scientific racism</a></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Unilineal_evolution" title="Unilineal evolution">Unilineal evolution</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Races_and_skulls.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="342" decoding="async" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Races_and_skulls.png/170px-Races_and_skulls.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Races_and_skulls.png/255px-Races_and_skulls.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Races_and_skulls.png/340px-Races_and_skulls.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Races_and_skulls.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Drawings from <a href="/wiki/Josiah_C._Nott" title="Josiah C. Nott">Josiah C. Nott</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Gliddon" title="George Gliddon">George Gliddon</a>'s <i>Indigenous races of the earth</i> (1857), which suggested <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">black people</a> ranked between <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">white people</a> and chimpanzees in terms of intelligence</div></div></div>
<p>The modern biological definition of race developed in the 19th century with scientific racist theories. The term <i>scientific racism</i> refers to the use of science to justify and support racist beliefs, which goes back to the early 18th century, though it gained most of its influence in the mid-19th century, during the <a href="/wiki/New_Imperialism" title="New Imperialism">New Imperialism</a> period. Also known as academic racism, such theories first needed to overcome the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Church</a>'s resistance to <a href="/wiki/Positivism" title="Positivism">positivist</a> accounts of history and its support of <a href="/wiki/Monogenism" title="Monogenism">monogenism</a>, the concept that all human beings were originated from the same ancestors, in accordance with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Creationist" title="Creationist">creationist</a> accounts of history.
</p><p>These racist theories put forth on scientific hypothesis were combined with <a href="/wiki/Unilineal_evolution" title="Unilineal evolution">unilineal theories of social progress</a>, which postulated the superiority of the European civilization over the rest of the world. Furthermore, they frequently made use of the idea of "<a href="/wiki/Survival_of_the_fittest" title="Survival of the fittest">survival of the fittest</a>", a term coined by <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Spencer" title="Herbert Spencer">Herbert Spencer</a> in 1864, associated with ideas of competition, which were named <a href="/wiki/Social_Darwinism" title="Social Darwinism">social Darwinism</a> in the 1940s. <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a> himself opposed the idea of rigid racial differences in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Descent_of_Man" title="The Descent of Man">The Descent of Man</a></i> (1871), in which he argued that humans were all of one species, sharing common descent. He recognised racial differences as varieties of humanity, and emphasised the close similarities between people of all races in mental faculties, tastes, dispositions and habits, while still contrasting the culture of the "lowest savages" with European civilization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dom_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-dom-237">[237]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the end of the 19th century, proponents of scientific racism intertwined themselves with <a href="/wiki/Eugenics" title="Eugenics">eugenics</a> discourses of "<a href="/wiki/Social_degeneration" title="Social degeneration">degeneration</a> of the race" and "blood <a href="/wiki/Heredity" title="Heredity">heredity</a>".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Henceforth, scientific racist discourses could be defined as the combination of polygenism, unilinealism, social Darwinism, and eugenism. They found their scientific legitimacy on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physical_anthropology" title="Physical anthropology">physical anthropology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthropometry" title="Anthropometry">anthropometry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Craniometry" title="Craniometry">craniometry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phrenology" title="Phrenology">phrenology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physiognomy" title="Physiognomy">physiognomy</a>, and others now discredited disciplines in order to formulate racist prejudices.
</p><p>Before being disqualified in the 20th century by the American school of <a href="/wiki/Cultural_anthropology" title="Cultural anthropology">cultural anthropology</a> (<a href="/wiki/Franz_Boas" title="Franz Boas">Franz Boas</a>, etc.), the British school of <a href="/wiki/Social_anthropology" title="Social anthropology">social anthropology</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bronis%C5%82aw_Malinowski" title="Bronisław Malinowski">Bronisław Malinowski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Radcliffe-Brown" title="Alfred Radcliffe-Brown">Alfred Radcliffe-Brown</a>, etc.), the French school of <a href="/wiki/Ethnology" title="Ethnology">ethnology</a> (<a href="/wiki/Claude_L%C3%A9vi-Strauss" title="Claude Lévi-Strauss">Claude Lévi-Strauss</a>, etc.), as well as the discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Modern_synthesis_(20th_century)" title="Modern synthesis (20th century)">neo-Darwinian synthesis</a>, such sciences, in particular anthropometry, were used to deduce behaviours and psychological characteristics from outward, physical appearances.
</p><p>The neo-Darwinian synthesis, first developed in the 1930s, eventually led to a <a href="/wiki/Gene-centered_view_of_evolution" title="Gene-centered view of evolution">gene-centered view of evolution</a> in the 1960s. According to the <a href="/wiki/Human_Genome_Project" title="Human Genome Project">Human Genome Project</a>, the most complete mapping of human DNA to date indicates that there is no clear <a href="/wiki/Race_and_genetics" title="Race and genetics">genetic basis to racial groups</a>. While some genes are more common in certain populations, there are no genes that exist in all members of one population and no members of any other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ornl_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-ornl-239">[239]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heredity_and_eugenics">Heredity and eugenics</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Eugenics" title="Eugenics">Eugenics</a></div>
<p>The first theory of <a href="/wiki/Eugenics" title="Eugenics">eugenics</a> was developed in 1869 by <a href="/wiki/Francis_Galton" title="Francis Galton">Francis Galton</a> (1822–1911), who used the then-popular concept of <i><a href="/wiki/Social_degeneration" title="Social degeneration">degeneration</a></i>. He applied <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">statistics</a> to study human differences and the alleged "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inheritance_of_intelligence" title="Inheritance of intelligence">inheritance of intelligence</a>", foreshadowing future uses of "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intelligence_testing" title="Intelligence testing">intelligence testing</a>" by the anthropometry school. Such theories were vividly described by the writer <a href="/wiki/%C3%89mile_Zola" title="Émile Zola">Émile Zola</a> (1840–1902), who started publishing in 1871, a twenty-novel cycle, <i><a href="/wiki/Les_Rougon-Macquart" title="Les Rougon-Macquart">Les Rougon-Macquart</a></i>, where he linked <a href="/wiki/Heredity" title="Heredity">heredity</a> to behavior. Thus, Zola described the high-born Rougons as those involved in politics (<i><a href="/wiki/Son_Excellence_Eug%C3%A8ne_Rougon" title="Son Excellence Eugène Rougon">Son Excellence Eugène Rougon</a></i>) and medicine (<i><a href="/wiki/Le_Docteur_Pascal" title="Le Docteur Pascal">Le Docteur Pascal</a></i>) and the low-born Macquarts as those fatally falling into <a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">alcoholism</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/L%27Assommoir" title="L'Assommoir">L'Assommoir</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Prostitution" title="Prostitution">prostitution</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Nana_(novel)" title="Nana (novel)">Nana</a></i>), and <a href="/wiki/Homicide" title="Homicide">homicide</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/La_B%C3%AAte_humaine" title="La Bête humaine">La Bête humaine</a></i>).
</p><p>During the rise of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazism in Germany</a>, some scientists in Western nations worked to debunk the regime's racial theories. A few argued against racist ideologies and discrimination, even if they believed in the alleged existence of biological races. However, in the fields of anthropology and biology, these were minority positions until the mid-20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> According to the 1950 UNESCO statement, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Race_Question" title="The Race Question">The Race Question</a></i>, an international project to debunk racist theories had been attempted in the mid-1930s. However, this project had been abandoned. Thus, in 1950, UNESCO declared that it had resumed:
</p>
<blockquote>
<p>...up again, after a lapse of fifteen years, a project that the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_on_Intellectual_Cooperation" title="International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation">International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation</a> has wished to carry through but that it had to abandon in deference to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Appeasement_of_Hitler" title="Appeasement of Hitler">appeasement policy</a> of the pre-war period. The race question had become one of the pivots of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nazi_ideology" title="Nazi ideology">Nazi ideology</a> and policy. <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1%C5%A1_Masaryk" title="Tomáš Masaryk">Masaryk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edvard_Bene%C5%A1" title="Edvard Beneš">Beneš</a> took the initiative of calling for a conference to re-establish in the minds and consciences of men everywhere the truth about race ... Nazi propaganda was able to continue its baleful work unopposed by the authority of an international organisation.
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_Reich%27s_racial_policies" title="Third Reich's racial policies">Third Reich's racial policies</a>, its <a href="/wiki/Nazi_eugenics" title="Nazi eugenics">eugenics programs</a> and the extermination of Jews in <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani people</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porrajmos" title="Porrajmos">Porrajmos</a> (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porajmos" title="Porajmos">Romani Holocaust</a>) and others minorities led to a change in opinions about scientific research into race after the war.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Changes within scientific disciplines, such as the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Franz_Boas" title="Franz Boas">Boasian</a> school of anthropology in the United States contributed to this shift. These theories were strongly denounced in the 1950 UNESCO statement, signed by internationally renowned scholars, and titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Race_Question" title="The Race Question">The Race Question</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Polygenism_and_racial_typologies">Polygenism and racial typologies</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Polygenism" title="Polygenism">Polygenism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Typology_(anthropology)" title="Typology (anthropology)">Typology (anthropology)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nordicism" title="Nordicism">Nordicism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Passing_of_the_Great_Race_-_Map_4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1533" data-file-width="2192" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Passing_of_the_Great_Race_-_Map_4.jpg/220px-Passing_of_the_Great_Race_-_Map_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Passing_of_the_Great_Race_-_Map_4.jpg/330px-Passing_of_the_Great_Race_-_Map_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Passing_of_the_Great_Race_-_Map_4.jpg/440px-Passing_of_the_Great_Race_-_Map_4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Passing_of_the_Great_Race_-_Map_4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Madison Grant's map, from 1916, charting the "present distribution of European races", with the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_race" title="Nordic race">Nordics</a> in red, the <a href="/wiki/Alpine_race" title="Alpine race">Alpines</a> in green, and the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_race" title="Mediterranean race">Mediterraneans</a> in yellow</div></div></div>
<p>Works such as <a href="/wiki/Arthur_de_Gobineau" title="Arthur de Gobineau">Arthur de Gobineau</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/An_Essay_on_the_Inequality_of_the_Human_Races" title="An Essay on the Inequality of the Human Races">An Essay on the Inequality of the Human Races</a></i> (1853–1855) may be considered one of the first theorizations of this new racism, founded on an essentialist notion of race, which opposed the former racial discourse, of <a href="/wiki/Henri_de_Boulainvilliers" title="Henri de Boulainvilliers">Boulainvilliers</a> for example, which saw in races a fundamentally historical reality, which changed over time. Gobineau, thus, attempted to frame racism within the terms of biological differences among humans, giving it the legitimacy of <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biology</a>.
</p><p>Gobineau's theories would be expanded in France by <a href="/wiki/Georges_Vacher_de_Lapouge" title="Georges Vacher de Lapouge">Georges Vacher de Lapouge</a> (1854–1936)'s <a href="/wiki/Typology_(anthropology)" title="Typology (anthropology)">typology of races</a>, who published in 1899 <i>The Aryan and his Social Role</i>, in which he claimed that the white "<a href="/wiki/Aryan" title="Aryan">Aryan</a> race" "<a href="/wiki/Cephalic_index" title="Cephalic index">dolichocephalic</a>", was opposed to the "brachycephalic" race, of whom the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jew" title="Jew">Jew</a>" was the archetype. Vacher de Lapouge thus created a <a href="/wiki/Hierarchical_classification" title="Hierarchical classification">hierarchical classification</a> of races, in which he identified the "<i><a href="/wiki/Nordic_race" title="Nordic race">Homo europaeus</a></i> (Teutonic, Protestant, etc.), the "<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homo_alpinus" title="Homo alpinus">Homo alpinus</a></i>" (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Auvergne_(province)" title="Auvergne (province)">Auvergnat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turkish</a>, etc.), and finally the "<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homo_mediterraneus" title="Homo mediterraneus">Homo mediterraneus</a></i>" (<a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Neapolitan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalus</a>, etc.) He assimilated races and <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">social classes</a>, considering that the French upper class was a representation of the <i>Homo europaeus</i>, while the lower class represented the <i>Homo alpinus</i>. Applying Galton's eugenics to his theory of races, Vacher de Lapouge's "selectionism" aimed first at achieving the annihilation of <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade unionists</a>, considered to be a "degenerate"; second, creating types of man each destined to one end, in order to prevent any contestation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labour_condition" title="Labour condition">labour conditions</a>. His "anthroposociology" thus aimed at blocking <a href="/wiki/Social_conflict" title="Social conflict">social conflict</a> by establishing a fixed, hierarchical social order.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup>
</p><p>The same year, <a href="/wiki/William_Z._Ripley" title="William Z. Ripley">William Z. Ripley</a> used identical racial classification in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Races_of_Europe_(Ripley)" title="The Races of Europe (Ripley)">The Races of Europe</a></i> (1899), which would have a great influence in the United States. Other scientific authors include <a href="/wiki/Houston_Stewart_Chamberlain" title="Houston Stewart Chamberlain">H.S. Chamberlain</a> at the end of the 19th century (a British citizen who <a href="/wiki/Naturalization" title="Naturalization">naturalized</a> himself as German because of his admiration for the "Aryan race") and <a href="/wiki/Madison_Grant" title="Madison Grant">Madison Grant</a>, a eugenicist and author of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Passing_of_the_Great_Race" title="The Passing of the Great Race">The Passing of the Great Race</a></i> (1916). Madison Grant provided statistics for the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_Act_of_1924" title="Immigration Act of 1924">Immigration Act of 1924</a>, which severely restricted immigration of Jews, <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a>, and Southern Europeans, who were subsequently hindered in seeking to escape Nazi Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_zoos">Human zoos</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Human_zoo" title="Human zoo">Human zoos</a> (called "People Shows"), were an important means of bolstering <i>popular racism</i> by connecting it to scientific racism: they were both objects of public curiosity and of <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthropometry" title="Anthropometry">anthropometry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joice_Heth" title="Joice Heth">Joice Heth</a>, an African-American slave, was displayed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phineas_Taylor_Barnum" title="Phineas Taylor Barnum">P.T. Barnum</a> in 1836, a few years after the exhibition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saartjie_Baartman" title="Saartjie Baartman">Saartjie Baartman</a>, the "Hottentot Venus", in England. Such exhibitions became common in the New Imperialism period, and remained so until World War II. <a href="/wiki/Carl_Hagenbeck" title="Carl Hagenbeck">Carl Hagenbeck</a>, inventor of the modern zoos, exhibited animals beside humans who were considered "savages".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diplo_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-Diplo-245">[245]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup>
</p><p>Congolese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pygmies" title="Pygmies">pygmy</a> <a href="/wiki/Ota_Benga" title="Ota Benga">Ota Benga</a> was displayed in 1906 by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eugenicist" title="Eugenicist">eugenicist</a> <a href="/wiki/Madison_Grant" title="Madison Grant">Madison Grant</a>, head of the <a href="/wiki/Bronx_Zoo" title="Bronx Zoo">Bronx Zoo</a>, as an attempt to illustrate the "missing link" between humans and <a href="/wiki/Orangutan" title="Orangutan">orangutans</a>: thus, racism was tied to <a href="/wiki/Darwinism" title="Darwinism">Darwinism</a>, creating a <a href="/wiki/Social_Darwinism" title="Social Darwinism">social Darwinist</a> ideology that tried to ground itself in <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Darwin</a>'s scientific discoveries. The 1931 Paris <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonial_Exhibition" title="Colonial Exhibition">Colonial Exhibition</a> displayed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kanaks" title="Kanaks">Kanaks</a> from <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> A "Congolese village" was on display as late as 1958 at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expo_%2758" title="Expo '58">Brussels' World Fair</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Theories_about_the_origins_of_racism">Theories about the origins of racism</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ethnocentrism" title="Ethnocentrism">Ethnocentrism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tribalism" title="Tribalism">Tribalism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Model_of_ethnic_%26_racial_conflict.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="488" data-file-width="1382" decoding="async" height="78" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Model_of_ethnic_%26_racial_conflict.png/220px-Model_of_ethnic_%26_racial_conflict.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Model_of_ethnic_%26_racial_conflict.png/330px-Model_of_ethnic_%26_racial_conflict.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Model_of_ethnic_%26_racial_conflict.png/440px-Model_of_ethnic_%26_racial_conflict.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Model_of_ethnic_%26_racial_conflict.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sociological model of ethnic and racial conflict</div></div></div>
<p>Evolutionary psychologists <a href="/wiki/John_Tooby" title="John Tooby">John Tooby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leda_Cosmides" title="Leda Cosmides">Leda Cosmides</a> were puzzled by the fact that in the US, race is one of the three characteristics most often used in brief descriptions of individuals (the others are age and sex). They reasoned that <a href="/wiki/Natural_selection" title="Natural selection">natural selection</a> would not have favoured the evolution of an instinct for using race as a classification, because for most of human history, humans almost never encountered members of other races. Tooby and Cosmides hypothesized that modern people use race as a proxy (rough-and-ready indicator) for coalition membership, since a better-than-random guess about "which side" another person is on will be helpful if one does not actually know in advance.
</p><p>Their colleague <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kurzban" title="Robert Kurzban">Robert Kurzban</a> designed an experiment whose results appeared to support this hypothesis. Using the <a href="/wiki/Memory_confusion_protocol" title="Memory confusion protocol">memory confusion protocol</a>, they presented subjects with pictures of individuals and sentences, allegedly spoken by these individuals, which presented two sides of a debate. The errors that the subjects made in recalling who said what indicated that they sometimes mis-attributed a statement to a speaker of the same race as the "correct" speaker, although they also sometimes mis-attributed a statement to a speaker "on the same side" as the "correct" speaker. In a second run of the experiment, the team also distinguished the "sides" in the debate by clothing of similar colors; and in this case the effect of racial similarity in causing mistakes almost vanished, being replaced by the color of their clothing. In other words, the first group of subjects, with no clues from clothing, used race as a visual guide to guessing who was on which side of the debate; the second group of subjects used the clothing color as their main visual clue, and the effect of race became very small.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KurzbanToobyCosmides2001ErasingRace_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-KurzbanToobyCosmides2001ErasingRace-248">[248]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some research suggests that ethnocentric thinking may have actually contributed to the development of cooperation. Political scientists Ross Hammond and Robert Axelrod created a computer simulation wherein virtual individuals were randomly assigned one of a variety of skin colors, and then one of a variety of trading strategies: be color-blind, favor those of your own color, or favor those of other colors. They found that the ethnocentric individuals clustered together, then grew, until all the non-ethnocentric individuals were wiped out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Selfish_Gene" title="The Selfish Gene">The Selfish Gene</a></i>, evolutionary biologist <a href="/wiki/Richard_Dawkins" title="Richard Dawkins">Richard Dawkins</a> writes that "Blood-feuds and inter-clan warfare are easily interpretable in terms of <a href="/wiki/W._D._Hamilton" title="W. D. Hamilton">Hamilton</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Kin_selection" title="Kin selection">genetic theory</a>." Dawkins writes that racial prejudice, while not evolutionarily adaptive, "could be interpreted as an irrational generalization of a kin-selected tendency to identify with individuals physically resembling oneself, and to be nasty to individuals different in appearance."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dawkins2006_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dawkins2006-250">[250]</a></sup> Simulation-based experiments in <a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_game_theory" title="Evolutionary game theory">evolutionary game theory</a> have attempted to provide an explanation for the selection of ethnocentric-strategy phenotypes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite support for evolutionary theories relating to an innate origin of racism, various studies have suggested racism is associated with lower intelligence and less diverse peer groups during childhood. A neuroimaging study on amygdala activity during racial matching activities found increased activity to be associated with adolescent age as well as less racially diverse peer groups, which the author conclude suggest a learned aspect of racism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> A meta analysis of neuroimaging studies found amygdala activity correlated to increased scores on implicit measures of racial bias. It was also argued amygdala activity in response to racial stimuli represents increased threat perception rather than the traditional theory of the amygdala activity represented ingroup-outgroup processing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> Racism has also been associated with lower childhood IQ in an analysis of 15,000 people in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="State-sponsored_racism">State-sponsored racism</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nazism_and_race" title="Nazism and race">Nazism and race</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racial_policy_of_Nazi_Germany" title="Racial policy of Nazi Germany">Racial policy of Nazi Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racial_antisemitism" title="Racial antisemitism">Racial antisemitism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eugenics_in_Showa_Japan" title="Eugenics in Showa Japan">Eugenics in Showa Japan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apartheid_in_South_Africa" title="Apartheid in South Africa">Apartheid in South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation_in_the_United_States" title="Racial segregation in the United States">Racial segregation in the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ketuanan_Melayu" title="Ketuanan Melayu">Ketuanan Melayu</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-Chinese_legislation_in_Indonesia" title="Anti-Chinese legislation in Indonesia">Anti-Chinese legislation in Indonesia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/White_Australia_policy" title="White Australia policy">White Australia policy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WhiteDoorColoredDoor.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2746" data-file-width="4114" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/WhiteDoorColoredDoor.jpg/220px-WhiteDoorColoredDoor.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/WhiteDoorColoredDoor.jpg/330px-WhiteDoorColoredDoor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/WhiteDoorColoredDoor.jpg/440px-WhiteDoorColoredDoor.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WhiteDoorColoredDoor.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Separate "white" and "colored" entrances to a café in <a href="/wiki/Durham,_North_Carolina" title="Durham, North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, 1940</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Neurenberger_Rassenwetten_NL.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2332" data-file-width="3328" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Neurenberger_Rassenwetten_NL.JPG/220px-Neurenberger_Rassenwetten_NL.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Neurenberger_Rassenwetten_NL.JPG/330px-Neurenberger_Rassenwetten_NL.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Neurenberger_Rassenwetten_NL.JPG/440px-Neurenberger_Rassenwetten_NL.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Neurenberger_Rassenwetten_NL.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1935 Chart from Nazi Germany used to explain the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">Nuremberg Laws</a>, defining which Germans were to be considered Jews and stripped of their citizenship. Germans with three or more Jewish grandparents were defined as Jews, Germans with one or two Jewish grandparents were deemed <i>Mischling</i> (mixed-blood).</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_racism" title="State racism">State racism</a>—that is, the institutions and practices of a nation-state that are grounded in racist ideology—has played a major role in all instances of <a href="/wiki/Settler_colonialism" title="Settler colonialism">settler colonialism</a>, from the United States to Australia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It also played a prominent role in the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi German</a> regime, in <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascist</a> regimes throughout Europe, and during the early years of Japan's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sh%C5%8Dwa_period" title="Shōwa period">Shōwa period</a>. These governments advocated and implemented ideologies and policies that were racist, xenophobic, and, in the case of <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a>, genocidal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">Nuremberg Race Laws</a> of 1935 prohibited sexual relations between any Aryan and Jew, considering it <i><a href="/wiki/Rassenschande" title="Rassenschande">Rassenschande</a></i>, "racial pollution". The Nuremberg Laws stripped all Jews, even quarter- and half-Jews (second and first degree <i>Mischlings</i>), of their German citizenship. This meant that they had no basic citizens' rights, e.g., the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_right_to_vote" title="The right to vote">right to vote</a>. In 1936, Jews were banned from all professional jobs, effectively preventing them from having any influence in education, politics, higher education, and industry. On 15 November 1938, Jewish children were banned from going to normal schools. By April 1939, nearly all Jewish companies had either collapsed under financial pressure and declining profits, or had been persuaded to sell out to the Nazi government. This further reduced their rights as human beings; they were in many ways officially separated from the German populace. Similar laws existed in Bulgaria—<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Law_for_protection_of_the_nation" title="Law for protection of the nation">The Law for protection of the nation</a>, Hungary, Romania, and Austria.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Chinese_Must_Go_-_Magic_Washer_-_1886_anti-Chinese_US_cartoon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2514" data-file-width="1836" decoding="async" height="301" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/The_Chinese_Must_Go_-_Magic_Washer_-_1886_anti-Chinese_US_cartoon.jpg/220px-The_Chinese_Must_Go_-_Magic_Washer_-_1886_anti-Chinese_US_cartoon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/The_Chinese_Must_Go_-_Magic_Washer_-_1886_anti-Chinese_US_cartoon.jpg/330px-The_Chinese_Must_Go_-_Magic_Washer_-_1886_anti-Chinese_US_cartoon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/The_Chinese_Must_Go_-_Magic_Washer_-_1886_anti-Chinese_US_cartoon.jpg/440px-The_Chinese_Must_Go_-_Magic_Washer_-_1886_anti-Chinese_US_cartoon.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Chinese_Must_Go_-_Magic_Washer_-_1886_anti-Chinese_US_cartoon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>19th century <a href="/wiki/Political_cartoon" title="Political cartoon">political cartoon</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/Uncle_Sam" title="Uncle Sam">Uncle Sam</a> kicks out the <a href="/wiki/Chinaman_(term)" title="Chinaman (term)">Chinaman</a></i>, referring to the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Exclusion_Act" title="Chinese Exclusion Act">Chinese Exclusion Act</a></div></div></div>
<p>Legislative state racism is known to have been enforced by the <a href="/wiki/National_Party_(South_Africa)" title="National Party (South Africa)">National Party</a> of South Africa during its <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">Apartheid</a> regime between 1948 and 1994. Here, a series of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apartheid_legislation_in_South_Africa" title="Apartheid legislation in South Africa">Apartheid legislation</a> was passed through the legal systems to make it legal for white South Africans to have rights which were superior to those of non-white South Africans. Non-white South Africans were not allowed involvement in any governing matters, including voting; access to quality healthcare; the provision of basic services, including clean water; electricity; as well as access to adequate schooling. Non-white South Africans were also prevented from accessing certain public areas, from using certain public transportation, and were required to live only in certain designated areas. Non-white South Africans were taxed differently than white South Africans and they were also required to carry on them at all times additional documentation, which later became known as "dom passes", to certify their non-white South African citizenship. All of these legislative racial laws were abolished through a series of equal <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> laws which were passed at the end of the Apartheid era in the early 1990s.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Anti-racism">Anti-racism</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Anti-racism" title="Anti-racism">Anti-racism</a></div>
<p>Anti-racism includes beliefs, actions, movements, and policies which are adopted or developed in order to oppose racism. In general, it promotes an egalitarian society in which people are not discriminated against on the basis of race. Examples of anti-racist movements include the <a href="/wiki/Civil_rights_movement" title="Civil rights movement">civil rights movement</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Apartheid_Movement" title="Anti-Apartheid Movement">Anti-Apartheid Movement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_Lives_Matter" title="Black Lives Matter">Black Lives Matter</a>. <a href="/wiki/Nonviolent_resistance" title="Nonviolent resistance">Nonviolent resistance</a> is sometimes embraced as an element of anti-racist movements, although this was not always the case. <a href="/wiki/Hate_crime" title="Hate crime">Hate crime</a> laws, <a href="/wiki/Affirmative_action" title="Affirmative action">affirmative action</a>, and bans on racist speech are also examples of government policy which is intended to suppress racism.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<li id="cite_note-Lieberman1997-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Lieberman1997_6-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1" id="CITEREFLieberman1997"><a href="/wiki/Leonard_Lieberman" title="Leonard Lieberman">Lieberman, Leonard</a> (1997). <a class="external text" href="http://s3.amazonaws.com/rdcms-aaa/files/production/public/FileDownloads/pdfs/cmtes/commissions/aec/upload/A_Race_Odyssey.pdf" rel="nofollow">"<span class="cs1-kern-left"></span>"Race" 1997 and 2001: A Race Odyssey"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <a href="/wiki/American_Anthropological_Association" title="American Anthropological Association">American Anthropological Association</a>. p. 2. <q>In the period since 1492, European overseas empires and colonies were established ... The establishment of mines and plantations enriched Europe while impoverishing and decimating the conquered and enslaved peoples in Africa and the New World. The race concept helped to give all this the appearance of scientific justification.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=%22Race%22+1997+and+2001%3A+A+Race+Odyssey&amp;rft.pages=2&amp;rft.pub=American+Anthropological+Association&amp;rft.date=1997&amp;rft.aulast=Lieberman&amp;rft.aufirst=Leonard&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fs3.amazonaws.com%2Frdcms-aaa%2Ffiles%2Fproduction%2Fpublic%2FFileDownloads%2Fpdfs%2Fcmtes%2Fcommissions%2Faec%2Fupload%2FA_Race_Odyssey.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARacism"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-120"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-120">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFEl_Hamel2002">El Hamel, Chouki (2002). "<span class="cs1-kern-left"></span>'Race', slavery and Islam in Maghribi Mediterranean thought: the question of the Haratin in Morocco". <i>The Journal of North African Studies</i>. <b>7</b> (3): 29–52 [39–40]. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1080%2F13629380208718472" rel="nofollow">10.1080/13629380208718472</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:219625829" rel="nofollow">219625829</a>. <q>Neither in the Qur'an nor in the <a href="/wiki/Hadith" title="Hadith">Hadith</a> is there any indication of racial difference among humankind. But as a consequence of the Arab conquests, a mutual assimilation between <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and the cultural and the scriptural traditions of Christian and Jewish populations occurred. Racial distinctions between humankind with reference to the <a href="/wiki/Generations_of_Noah" title="Generations of Noah">sons of Noah</a> is found in the <a href="/wiki/Talmud" title="Talmud">Babylonian Talmud</a>, a collection of rabbinic writings which dates back to the sixth century.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Journal+of+North+African+Studies&amp;rft.atitle=%27Race%27%2C+slavery+and+Islam+in+Maghribi+Mediterranean+thought%3A+the+question+of+the+Haratin+in+Morocco&amp;rft.volume=7&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.pages=29-52+39-40&amp;rft.date=2002&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1080%2F13629380208718472&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A219625829%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft.aulast=El+Hamel&amp;rft.aufirst=Chouki&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARacism"></span></span>
</li>
